< Review>
I walked across the street from my dry cleaning spot and have been wanting to try this taqueria.

I didn‚Äôt expect much since I am a self proclaimed taco fanatic and I usually am disappointed with dry carne asada.

The restaurant was clean. The tacos were a hefty size. The carne asada was dripping with flavor and so so tender. I am wildly surprised and am so happy I finally went in after looking at this restaurant every time I drop off my clothes. The carnitas were delicious as well but the real winner was the carne asada.

The person who took my order was extremely friendly and made sure I knew I could take chips if I wanted them. Also the salsa rojo is medium spicy and had a nice kick!

Can‚Äôt wait to come back now that I know I have a delicious neighborhood taco spot.</Review>

<Rating>4</Rating>< Review>
The WiFi is acceptable. For Irvine, that is mandatory at minimum, especially being this close to University of California Irvine.

Came in here recently on a work from home day as I had an errand earlier that day to run. After finding a table close to a power AC outlet, I plugged my laptop in and started crunching some infrastructure-as-code.

This cafe is well ventilated which is really important during hot Irvine summers, which speaks to how well the HVAC systems are here. That's a damn good thing.

Located in University Center, if you need to stand up for a stretch break, there are plenty of places to swing by nearby, including but not limited to: Eureka, Gen Grill, Amazon Prime at Irvine, Slap Fish, Blaze Pizza, even a United States Post Office! There are options a-plenty here.

Drinks here are ok. Noticed I saved drinks for last? It's actually not anything spectacular but nothing terrible either.

Oh and they take mobile payments here like Apple and Google Pay.<//Review>

<rating>4</rating>< text>
I was starving for Vietnamese food and my friends suggested to go here on a Wednesday for lunch! We walked in right as they opened and I couldn't have been happier!!!

Our waiter was very attentive and brought us water and menus immediately. I felt like the ambiance throughout the restaurant was very dim and set more for the dinner folks. But we seated ourselves along the windows close to the entrance to give ourselves a brighter vibe. The three of us ended up ordering the BBQ pork with imperial rolls and all with rice instead of vermicelli. And oh dear, the portion was delicious and HUGE!

The BBQ pork itself was juicy on the inside and had a lovely crust of BBQ char. It came along with three miniature rolls of fried imperial rolls that cannot disappoint. It was extremely crispy on the outside and that's the most important part! Lastly, the rice was super moist and fluffy just the way I like it! The portion was huge but it was so good that I ate the entire thing in one sitting. I had no regrets though, and you won't either!

I also had a thai iced tea that I felt was sweetened perfectly for my sweet tooth and the dish and the drink totaled to be $14! I wish that I worked close by so that I could eat here all the time!< /text>

< text>
Six months ago we moved in just a few steps away from the restaurant and finally decided to try it today.
We've read the reviews, saw the high grade and our expectations were high.

Not sure what happened.

The first thing that hit us is the unpleasant smell. It's not our first Vietnamese restaurant, and you expect the smell of spices and flavors that you are less familiar with, but in this case, it was acidic and unpleasant.
Even though the place was only half full, the waiters were really impatient with us with a great sense of urgency that was very unclear.
For an appetizer, we chose the imperial rolls. Pretty good, but clearly heated in a microwave and not very fresh. The Garlic noodles were very mediocre and uninspiring. Jasmine garden noodle soup was ok-ish but .. I don't know.
I've seen the reviews on this website, and on few others. The average grade is ~4.5 or so. I really wish I felt it deserved even a 3 star.
The service is unfriendly, the food is not fresh (some it at least) and I'm not coming back.
Maybe it's just me, I don't know.< /text>

< Review>
I LOVE this place. I'm a total regular. Here is why.

BEST vegetarian pho in the city, hands down!

I get the vegetarian pho with a side of the spicy lemongrass sauce to put in it. It is the tastiest veggie pho I've ever had and it's packed with veggies like mushrooms, bok choy, carrots, broccoli, fresh cilantro, and tofu. They also have a delicious lemon grass tofu over vermicelli (over rice on the menu). It comes with crushed peanuts and a salad on the bottom. The ingredients are fresh, always, and the service is great. I love the people who work there, especially the woman server (i think she may be one of the owners?) who always remembers me and is really warm and speedy. It's also cheap! I always walk out with a full belly and feel surprised at how little money it is. I highly recommend this spot- they also deliver!

Negatives: not organic, if someone knows of an organic pho spot-please let me know!

<Review>San Francisco is blessed with a good amount of decent Vietnamese restaurants and Jasmine Garden fits perfectly in. An inexpensive menu with quality items, a welcoming interior and friendly staff. What more can you ask for?

If you're not in the mood for pho try one of their noodle plates or com dia (rice dishes).

My favorite here is the VEGETABLE PHO ($7.95) - the broth is a little bit on the sweeter side and extremely delicious. The BEEF PHO ($8.95) is also very good, with thin beef slices in a very flavorful soup.

The restaurant is frequented by single diners and groups alike, and the food comes out very fast.

Love the service, the prices, and the food - one of my favorite pho places in town.</Review>< user_name>
Sebastian Fiedler<//user_name>

<Date>1392058343937</Date><rate>4</rate><review>Ah the food of my homeland. Cue the asian string instruments. This is a review that will help your experience at Jasmine Garden. First tip, how do you pronounce "Pho"? Pretend you are saying the F-word, but remove the "ck". Stop saying "Foah".

On to the review. First off, in my experience, the waiter here will not give you the Pho menu. They will give you another menu that's missing the Pho. My guess is that they want you to get the higher priced seafood dishes? Anyways, you may have to ask for the pho menu, which is exactly like the other with one more page.

I recommend the Pho Dac Biet (Means the Pho special). That has beef. They also have a Vegetarian Pho that's good (You shouldn't be getting this if you can eat meat). The imperial rolls were really good too. I like mine with extra lettuce.

Overall great Vietnamese restaurant in SF. Best part you don't have to go to Little Saigon to get good Vietnamese food anymore.</review><Pics>None<//Pics>< response>
None< /response>

</dataset><record>
<UserId.>110755156016415798072<//UserId.><Name>Roy Chi< /Name>< Time>
1378861788617<//Time>
<rate>4<//rate>< Review>
Jasmine Garden is definitely one of the best Vietnamese restaurants in SF, just as long as you're NOT eating pho.

The Pho here has way too much cinnamon. It was like an apple cider broth. The beef slices were tough and the broth just isn't hot enough. Everything about this pho was lackluster and not even worth serving at what is otherwise an amazing Vietnamese restaurant.

-----------------------
FOOD:

Catfish Sweet & Sour Soup =
Incredible. A perfect blend of sweet and sour that goes extremely well with white rice.

Banh Xeo =
Crispy and flavorful, I loved this Banh Xeo.

Raw Beef Slices =
Delicious. The mixture of the cilantro, peanuts, and fish sauce made these tender raw beef slices amazing.

Chicken & Shrimp Salad =
This was okay. There wasn't much flavor in this dish -- had to drench it in fish sauce.

Shaking Beef =
The Shaking Beef here was tender, but the flavor was a bit off. It was still good, just a bit sour from the vinegar in the sauce.

Deep-Fried Shrimp w/ Garlic Noodles =
Shrimp should have been a bit more deep-fried, but the garlic noodles were EXCELLENT here.

Sea Bass over Glass Noodle =
This dish was just okay. The sea bass was a bit TOO flaky and the glass noodles were too garlicky. It went pretty well with white rice (since there was so much pungency from the garlic), though.

Roasted Quail =
Excellent quail. It came out bursting with flames (from the Bacardi 151 that it was doused in) and had tons of flavor.

-----------------------------

Jasmine Garden is one of the more authentic Vietnamese restaurants I've been to in SF. With the serious exception of their horrible pho, Jasmine Garden is an amazing Vietnamese restaurant that will guarantee a great experience.</Review>
